# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Django ORM Raw SQL Injection Prevention

## Your Task

Find all Python source files in django/django that handle raw SQL queries and prevent SQL injection: the RawSQL expression sanitization, the raw() queryset method parameter binding, and the cursor.execute() parameterization enforcement.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the security domain.

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/django--674eda1c.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/django--674eda1c` (django/django)

77-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've created a comprehensive answer documenting all the Python source files in django/django that handle raw SQL queries and prevent SQL injection. Here's a summary of my findings:

## Key Findings

**SQL Injection Prevention Architecture:**

1. **RawSQL Expression** (django/db/models/expressions.py) - Enforces separation of SQL code from parameters at the expression level

2. **Parameter Binding in QuerySet.raw()** (django/db/models/query.py) - Maintains parameter separation through the query pipeline via RawQuerySet → RawQuery

3. **Cursor.execute() Parameterization** (django/db/models/sql/query.py) - RawQuery._execute_query() adapts parameters and passes them separately to cursor.execute()

4. **CursorWrapper System** (django/db/backends/utils.py) - Wraps all database execution, passing SQL and parameters separately with support for execution hooks

5. **Backend-Specific Protection:**
   - **SQLite** (sqlite3/base.py) - SQLiteCursorWrapper converts parameter styles while maintaining separation
   - **PostgreSQL** (postgresql/base.py) - ServerBindingCursor and Cursor classes support server-side and client-side parameter binding
   - **Oracle** (oracle/base.py) - OracleParam with bind_parameter() for late-binding cursor variables

6. **Parameter Type Adaptation** (django/db/backends/base/operations.py) - adapt_unknown_value() converts Python types to database-compatible types safely

The answer.json file has been created at `/workspace/answer.json` with all files, symbols, and a detailed narrative explaining Django's multi-layered SQL injection prevention mechanisms.

It requires developers to pass SQL and parameters separately: `RawSQL(sql, params, output_field=None)`. The params argument is mandatory and cannot be omitted, forcing developers to acknowledge they are using parameterization.\\n\\n## Raw QuerySet Method Parameter Binding\\n\\nThe **QuerySet.raw()** method (django/db/models/query.py:1461-1473) accepts raw_query and params arguments separately. This method creates a RawQuerySet instance that passes both the SQL string and parameters through the execution pipeline without interpolating them together.\\n\\nThe **RawQuerySet** class (django/db/models/query.py:2285-2350) stores the raw SQL query and parameters separately, maintaining this separation throughout the object's lifetime.\\n\\n## Cursor.execute() Parameterization Enforcement\\n\\nThe critical execution point is in **RawQuery._execute_query()** (django/db/models/sql/query.py:208-225), which:\\n\\n1. wrappers while maintaining parameter separation\\n\\n## Backend-Specific Parameter Handling\\n\\nEach database backend implements parameter binding protection:\\n\\n**SQLite** \\\"named\\\")\\n- **execute()** and **executemany()** methods (lines 353-370) perform parameter style conversion while maintaining separation\\n- **convert_query()** method (lines 372-378) safely using psycopg3\\n- **Cursor** uses client-side parameter binding with psycopg3/psycopg2\\n- **ServerSideCursor** for named cursor support with client-side binding enforcement\\n\\n**Oracle** (django/db/backends/utils.py:117-150) wraps cursor execution for debugging while maintaining parameter separation through the `debug_sql()` context manager.\\n\\nAll execution goes through
